I've been cutting my own hair for probably over a year now using the [[ASIN:B002C741MW Philips Norelco QC5170 180-Degree Hair Clipper]] so naturally I was excited to try this do-it-yourself hair clipper. After a few haircuts, though, I must say that I can't really tell that much of a difference. When comparing the two, the only significant difference I could find was that this model is washable.<br /><br />So, if you've seen the two models and aren't sure what to get, well then I guess this one is better for the washability because both seem to work well. Here's my list of pros and cons, which (with few exceptions) applies to both.<br /><br />Pros:<br />- Cuts very well. I have thick hair so I was nervous that a wireless clipper wasn't going to be able to actually cut like a professional. It does. Sometimes you gotta go over the same spot a few times to make sure everything is even, but otherwise, this beast could shave you bald in a matter of seconds. Also, I'm quite impressed that the blades have stayed strong and sharp even after a year of use.<br /><br />- 180 degree angle. I wouldn't necessarily call this feature THE selling point, but occasionally I find adjusting the angle to be beneficial in getting odd areas of hair. 90% of the time I just keep it upright, though.<br /><br />- \\"Adjustable zoom ring\\" - I really like that there are so many length possibilities. Personally I prefer the 1 - 5 numbers on the QC5170, but the same concept is featured here and it lets you play around with how close or unclose you want the clipper to shave.<br /><br />- Good charge life. Not GREAT charge life, but the good news is that it will function as fully charged until it goes out so even if the battery is half dead it won't be running on half power. Considering that haircuts are a fairly sporadic event, I couldn't imagine anyone having a really severe problem with the battery life unless they just forgot to charge it after a month or something.<br /><br />Cons<br /><br />- Limited hair styles. You get a lot of different length options, but in the case of my unprofessional knowledge of hair cutting, it would be hard for me to imagine anyone giving themselves a truly awesome hair-do that wasn't a buzz. I mean, you can do a lot of touching up and such, but for an all over cut - I wouldn't necessarily invest in this unless you know someone who can help you with it or unless you like a simple short cut like I do.<br /><br />Overall - I must say, if you're in any way interested in cutting back on unnecessary spending, this personal hair clipper may be a great way to save a lot of money. As long as you aren't especially picky about a certain style, you can easily give yourself a decent variety of simple looks that will in no way scream unprofessional. I've had great experiences with Philips Norelco products, including the other model of hair clipper and their bodygrooms so I would definitely stand by the brand.length options, but in the case of my unprofessional knowledge of hair cutting, it would be hard for me to imagine anyone giving themselves a truly awesome hair-do that wasn't a buzz. I mean, you can do a lot of touching up and such, but for an all over cut - I wouldn't necessarily invest in this unless you know someone who can help you with it or unless you like a simple short cut like I do. Overall - I must say, if you're in any way interested in cutting back on unnecessary spending, this personal hair clipper may be a great way to save a lot of money. I've had great experiences with Philips Norelco products, including the other model of hair clipper and their bodygrooms so I would definitely stand by the brand.

  27. This is great for a beard, and anything you want to clip with a size 1 clipper setting or lower. However, once you get into the longer clipper extensions (anything above a 1), it's not so great. It's a bit difficult to describe the issue without seeing it, but the way this is designed, there is a space between the clipper blades, and the plastic clipper guide that determines how long the hair will be. The problem with that is, if you exert pressure on the clippers towards your head (which you must), the clipping guide is pressed towards the clippers... meaning it'll cut a bit closer. If it were just a little bit, i wouldn't mind, but it makes a significant difference, so you really have to try to perfectly balance the amount of pressure you exert on your head.<br /><br />The other issue is, after using this for several months, the clippers don't always stay at the same setting. Sometimes I'll be clipping at a 4, and then realize that I pressed a little too hard and the setting slid down to a 3. It's not bending... but pushing the whole trimmer down a notch. I wound up having to shave my head MUCH closer than I wanted to this time.<br /><br />I'm disappointed that this didn't last longer because they worked great for the first several months.<br /><br />I think i'm going for Andis clippers next time, or something else with replaceable blades. They're more expensive, but they are supposed to last forever. I'm tired of swapping between various cheaper clippers and wasting money.<br /><br />Revision: I just changed my rating from a 3 star to 1 star because 2 of the clipper guides they gave me broke (The smallest, and the mid size extensions). It was quite unfortunate as both broke while I was using them... not fun!   58. I love the concept of this hair clipper... unfortunately it's implementation makes it one of the worst trimmers I've ever owned. As I see it, there are two key problems: the motor and the motor attachment. First, it seems like Philips took the motor out of a standard face shaver and stuck it in a hair clip... this is a terrible idea! Simply put, this unit doesn't have the torque to cut through anything but the thinnest / shortest hair. It regularly gets caught in my moderately-thick hair, which brings me to the second problem.<br /><br />This unit translates the rotational power of the motor into linear motion via a metal pin driving a plastic wedge. The strain of cutting the hair is put on a cheap plastic component, being driving by a metal one. The result? Half way through my first haircut, the clipper starting making a terrible squeal. I immediately stopped it, cleaned it, and went back to work. A few minutes later, the same thing happened. This time, I took it apart to see what the issue was... the aforementioned plastic component had been ground down to nearly nothing! By the second haircut, I had to throw the unit out... the critical plastic component had literally been ground away.<br /><br />In short, this thing is woefully underpowered and cheaply made. I got exactly 1.5 haircuts out of it before it irrevocably broke.

  152. I have been using this cutter for about two months now and am very pleased with the results. It has saved me a lot of time and money. It works particularly well with short to medium hairstyles. Here are some tips that I have learned:<br /><br />When you first get this product take the time to carefully read the instructions and try out all of the parts, particularly try fitting the combs and adjusting the heights.<br /><br />For the first few times you use this product, plan what you intend to do before you start cutting. For example, Pick a comb and length setting for the top of your head, the back, the sides, and around the ears. Also pick an order to do your cutting. It can be from top down or bottom up. For your first haircut, use slightly longer settings to make sure you are cutting the way you want. After your first cut, you might want to \\"even up\\" the next day to get the hang of your final routine for cutting.<br /><br />You will quickly get the hang of using this cutter and settle into the settings you want for each part of your head and the most effective order of cutting. You should jot these settings down for future haircuts.<br /><br />When you cut using the flexible cutters use only a light pressure and, as the instructions say, run the cutter back and forth from different angles for an even cut. It is really quite easy and the only trick is making sure you are using the right comb and height for the area you are cutting.<br /><br />To keep things simple, I have not used to the rotating head but you may want to try it out.<br /><br />The cordless feature is a big improvement over a cord. For easy cleanup, I use it either in my bathtub or shower (this makes cleanup very easy since I can then continue with a bath or shower).<br /><br />A cutter charge time is very quick and it will last through several haircuts. And it is very easy to use this cutter for quick trims.<br /><br />Highly recommended!!<br /><br />edit:<br /><br />Still highly recommended!!You may want to skip using the rotating head. I found it is no real use because your haircut is more effective if you are using the cutter from different angles, as recommended in the instructions. Because you have no cord, angling the cutter is really very easy and switching hands, which you have to do anyway, is no big deal. It also saves you time when you don't bother rotating the head.

  284. If you allow the conceit that hair clippers designed for the home market have the commercial heft and market dynamism necessary to ever be classifiable as \\"game changers\\" , then this hair clipper is such a specimen.<br /><br />I long ago gave up on trying to elicit from any hair stylist in any price range any interest in my hair. To say that it has a will of its own would be like saying Jocelyn Wildenstein has had some plastic surgery. It's out of control and who can blame anyone with a professional reputation at stake for withholding their energy and talent from something which, with only the briefest glance of their trained eye, can be immediately classified as \\"destined to be train wreck\\" ?<br /><br />Not me.<br /><br />So I cut my own hair, and, like people with normal hair, earnestly wish each every time for a good outcome. Consequently I have had very many of these things over the years, usually Wahls as I recall, and sometimes ConAir.<br /><br />Here is why this is much much better than those.<br /><br />There are no little colored clipper heads to lose, corral, contain, break, become annoyed with or be radically over charged for. Instead, there is clearly labeled and easy to use dial that raises and lowers the clipper head and is an effective rebuttal to the \\"multitude of clipper heads\\" approach. There are just two clipper heads, but for everything but the closest trim, the main one will do .<br /><br />The clipper head itself rotates 180 degrees (or more perhaps) . What this means is when you do the OTHER side of your head, you don't have to hold your arm at an awkward, Yogi-like angle. The clipper head rotates (instead of your arm) and the result is it's nearly as easy to accurately cut the hair on your non-dominate side as it is your dominate side. It's great.<br /><br />It's built-in battery driven / rechargeable and the charge lasts for at least two or three haircuts, not less, meaning you aren't going to be stuck in the middle of a hair cut with no juice. What's more- there's no cord to get in your way, or markedly increase the footprint of the clipper, or tether you like a wayward cow to a circle of radius 4 feet about your outlet, or cramp your arm's approach to your hair or knock the lamp off your dresser as you reach for the back of your hair with your clipper.<br /><br />It charges very quickly and plugs directly into the wall, no cradle or anything like that is involved. You don't have another electric cord to label and keep somewhere.<br /><br />It's well built, well designed and I expect it will last years. You never need to oil it; the lubrication is self contained. The space I have dedicated to my hair clipper just got cut by 2/3rds. That alone is almost worth the price of admission.<br /><br />Finally, you clean this thing by holding it under running water (after it's turned off) . That's right, the manufacturer designed this thing to be cleanable with running water. It comes clean very easily.<br /><br />Here are some tips .<br /><br />The head is unlike other heads on clippers. It comes on and off very easily, but it's not immediately obvious how, by which I mean, you have to read the (very clear) instructions, otherwise, like me, you're likely to apply too much pressure trying to get it off in some way it doesn't really come off, but looks like it might. If you're applying pressure, you're doing it wrong.<br /><br />The head rotates so that as you go around your hair, you can always have the same angle of attack. Just exactly how to rotate the head is hard to describe and for me, it was counter-intuitive. I got it wrong the first time; here's what I can offer by way of advice: if it seems not *quite* right, rotate the head the OTHER way.<br /><br />I look at it this way; I save a lot of money cutting my own hair. This clipper makes that process more effective, easier, less time consuming and a heck of a lot less cluttered. It's just a cleaner faster crisper process. The difference in pricebetween the rock bottom regular style hair clipper and this one is a fraction of what I'm saving overall. If it were 100 bucks I'd say it's not worth it, go coach. But for 20 bucks or so more, it's worth it.

  292. The clipper works but there's a major design flaw with the contour comb that is easily fixed. If you read some other reviews they state that the comb is only even at the lowest level. This is because the contour comb changes the hair length depending on the angle. If you read the product description it says \\"2-D Contour-<br />Following Comb \\". If it were at least well designed this wouldn't be a problem but it is.<br /><br />I uploaded a customer photo that illustrates the difference in height as the comb moves. With the parallel lines added you can clearly see the difference in height. The higher the angle, the shorter the cut, which messes up the hair length. The difference in height is only around 6-7mm but that's a lot and more than enough to mess up your haircut.<br /><br />By fixing the comb angle it'll cut hair to a consistent length. If your combs are already used, wash the combs with rubbing alcohol and hot water to clean off hair oils. A clean surface will help the glue stick better.<br /><br />Solution:<br />1. pull out the end of the small spring that holds the comb in the neutral position - you want the comb flat and don't want it putting pressure on the comb while you glue it. The spring is not used anymore so you can cut it or pull it out.<br />2. Superglue the rear of the comb to the base so that it's flat and hold it tight while the glue sets.<br />3. Superglue the hinges until you see that it's full of glue. The plastic is clear so you can see the hinge filling up with glue.<br />4. Enjoy! Obviously this will void the warranty on the comb.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the middle comb is slightly flexible so if you press too hard it'll bow in at the middle. This can also mess up the hair length. You just have to not press too hard. If the comb was made of stronger plastic and it didn't have this horribly designed contour comb, I would have rated it 4 stars.<br /><br />The rest of the review: Charge life is good, I didn't run out of juice but I only ran it while actually clipping my hair, not just constantly on. I used to use a corded clipper and the hardest part was cutting the back and top-back of my head. I had to hold the mirror with one hand and angle your other arm just right. The swivel head fixed this issue. I noticed that I had to make a few more passes to get my hair even vs. my corded clipper but the ease of doing the back is worth the trade off. Combined with the comb design flaw, it bumped my rating down to 3 stars.<br /><br />As with any other clippers, if you want medium length hair on the top you still have to use scissors and use clippers on the rear-sides.

  321. Seldom do I review anything from Amazon. This handy little hair clipper is an exception.<br /><br />Before purchasing the clippers, I got my hair cut whenever my wife went to see her stylist; about every 6 weeks. Typically we're booked for an hour, of which it took the stylist just 5-10 minutes to cut my hair with electric clippers and scissors to trim around the ears.<br /><br />With these clippers I'm able to cut my hair more often, which means less annoyance with my hair, having reached that age where I can't stand hair over my ears, not to mention the hair now growing from the tops of my ears. It takes about 20 minutes to give myself a haircut that's every bit as good as the $22 cut from my wife's stylist. Having retired recently, we appreciate saving the cost of a stylist, which leaves more money for travel and entertainment. In just 4 uses, these clippers have already paid for themselves twice over.<br /><br />It does however take some planning to minimize the mess and I've come up with a system that works well for me.<br /><br />Before cutting my hair, I charge the clipper and lay it out with the attachments, a neck duster brush, a glass of water, a comb and hand-held mirror, next to the bathtub. Just before cutting my hair, I shower, wash my hair, dry off and comb my hair to stand upright. To cut my hair, I sit on the side of the tub with my feet in the tub, so the hair will fall into the tub when cut.<br /><br />Having cut my hair with these clippers several times, I find it best to cut the top first with the large attachment, set on 8. It's best to cut front to back, left to right, back to front, and right to left to ensure an even cut, rotating the cutting head as needed for ease of use. Since the sides are shorter, it's OK to run the clipper over and around the crown, since the long setting won't cut any hair shorter than the setting. When there is no more hair falling into the tub at my feet, I use the mirror and a comb wetted in the glass of water to comb my hair upright and check for any tufts that might have been missed. But that's never been a problem when cutting the hair from every direction. There is however a single hair every once in awhile that needs another pass of the clippers.<br /><br />Once the top is cut, I change to the smaller attachment and set it for 3-1/2. To ensure the shorter hair on the sides blend into the longer hair on top, I cut from bottom to top and when reaching the curve of the crown, continue upward in a straight line. If I were to follow the crown curve around to the top of my head, it would leave an obvious step where the 2 lengths meet. In this way, the sides and top blend naturally. Once again, rotate the head as necessary for ease of use, and go over the sides from bottom up, front to back and back to front for an even cut.<br /><br />The only difficulty with self administered hair cuts, is trimming around the ears and the back of the neck. My wife makes quick work of the fine trimming, after removing the length adapters from the trimmer and cutting with the bare cutting edge. For the detail work, the [[ASIN:B0001KBP7G Neck Duster #64 Long Handle]], comes in very handy.<br /><br />Once done, use toilet paper to pick up the cut hair from the floor of the bathtub and flush it down the toilet. The remaining hair is easily washed down the drain with the hand held shower attachment.<br /><br />Afterward, I shower and wash my hair again to rinse the last of the hair down the drain. Washing my hair again after cutting has an additional benefit I appreciate. For whatever reason, my scalp often broke out after a haircut with the stylist. Since cutting my own hair and washing before and after cutting, there has been no recurrence of scalp breakout.<br /><br />The method I use to cut my hair makes a hair cutting cape unnecessary. I do not advocate cutting hair they way I do with conventional plug-in clippers, for obvious electrical safety reasons.
